<script>
	function goToTopic(topic) {
		var topicMap = applySpecialCharacterMapping(topic); 
		var url = "/xpl/topicbrowse.jsp?topic=" + escape(topicMap);
		window.top.location.href = url;
	}
</script>

			<!-- ngIf: ::vm.details.abstract --><div ng-if="::vm.details.abstract" class="ng-scope">
				<strong>Abstract:</strong>
				<div class="abstract-text ng-binding" ng-bind-html="::vm.details.abstract">In this paper, an experimental methodology for the characterization of the impedance of balanced RF identification (RFID) tag antennas is presented, and the application of the proposed method in RFID tag co-design is demonstrated. The balanced tag antenna is considered as a two-port network and the impedance of the antenna is characterized using network parameters. In the measurement, the antenna is connected to the two ports of a vector network analyzer through a test fixture. The influence of the test fixture is deembedded by using a port-extension technique and the antenna impedance can be extracted directly from the measured S -parameters. The proposed method is useful in practical RFID applications for co-designing the RFID tag with the attached platforms for enhancing the tag performance. An example of co-designing an ultra-high-frequency RFID tag with a plastic Sushi plate is demonstrated. The co-designed tag antenna achieves conjugate matching with the application-specific integrated circuit so that the reading range of the RFID tag is greatly enhanced.</div>
			</div><!-- end ngIf: ::vm.details.abstract -->			
			<!-- ngIf: ::vm.details.scope -->
			<!-- ngIf: ::vm.details.purpose -->

<div id="BodyWrapper" class="ArticlePage" xmlns:ieee="http://www.ieeexplore.ieee.org"><div id="article">
<div class="section" id="sec1"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION I.</div><h2>Introduction</h2></div><p>Generally, an RF identification (RFID) tag antenna is designed for an application-specific integrated circuit (ASIC) available in the market. The ASIC is usually placed right at the terminals of a balanced tag antenna. Using an additional matching circuit with lumped elements is usually prohibitive due to cost and fabrication issues. Therefore, proper impedance matching between the antenna and the ASIC is of paramount importance for tag design. The tag antenna and the ASIC are required to be conjugate matched for maximum power transfer in order to achieve maximum read range <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_1">[1]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a>.</p><p>In RFID applications, RFID tags are always affixed to platforms, which feature widely varying size, electrical properties, and material composition. The input impedance of the tag antennas is thus affected by the platforms. The change of the antenna impedance results in the mismatch between the tag antenna and the ASIC chip so that the performance of the tag is degraded <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a>â<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_1">[4]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a>. The effects of the platforms on the antenna impedance can be alleviated by using platform tolerant tag antennas with larger ground plane <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_1">[6]</a>â<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_1">[7]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_1">[8]</a>. However, the platform tolerant tag antennas may not be applicable in some applications where size constraint is a critical issue. Alternatively, the tag performance can be improved by co-designing the tag taking the electrical/physical properties of the platforms into account. However, it is difficult to accurately predict the impedance variation of the tag antennas in a real environment from simulation due to the complicated application scenarios and the uncertainty of the electrical properties of the attached platforms. The experimental method is a more practical way to characterize the tag antenna impedance accurately.</p><p>In this paper, an experimental methodology for the impedance characterization of balanced RFID tag antennas is presented. The proposed methodology is applied to the co-design of an ultra-high-frequency (UHF) RFID tag for the plate tracking in a Sushi restaurant. The impedance of the tag antenna which is attached to a plastic Sushi plate can be measured accurately with the proposed method. This allows the tag antenna to achieve better conjugate matching with the ASIC. Therefore, the significant enhancement of read range of the co-designed RFID tag can be realized.</p><p>This paper is organized as follows. <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec2" class="fulltext-link">SectionÂ II</a> describes the methodology of the balanced antenna impedance characterization. The validation of the methodology is carried out in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec3" class="fulltext-link">SectionÂ III</a>, where the comparison of the measured and calculated impedance of an asymmetrical dipole antenna and a symmetrical meander line dipole antenna is exhibited. <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec4" class="fulltext-link">SectionÂ IV</a> demonstrates the example of using the proposed methodology for co-designing and optimizing a UHF RFID tag. Finally, conclusions are given in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec5" class="fulltext-link">SectionÂ V</a>.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec2"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION II.</div><h2>Impedance Characterization Methodology</h2></div><p>The majority of the RFID tag antennas are balanced designs. The impedance of a balanced antenna cannot be measured directly by most measurement instruments which are terminated with unbalanced ports such as coaxial ports. When a balanced antenna is connected to an unbalanced test port, the currents fed to the two radiators of the antenna are unequal, and thus, the impedance of the balanced antenna cannot be characterized accurately. Traditionally, the impedance of a balanced antenna can be measured by using a balun, which forces the equal currents to flow in each parts of the antenna radiator. However, the accuracy of such measurement results relies on how ideal the balun is, especially over a wide testing frequency band. The impedance of a symmetrical balanced antenna can also be measured using imaging method, i.e., mounting half part of the radiators of the antenna on a ground plane, which provides a mirror imaging to configure the other part of radiators. The impedance of the antenna can be obtained by multiplying a factor of 2 of the measured impedance of the equivalent monopole. However, the accuracy of the measurement results is much dependent on the size of the ground plane used, and this method is valid only for symmetrical balanced antennas <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_2">[9]</a>.</p><p>Different from classic ways, Meys et al. presented an <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-1-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 0.664em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.604em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.6em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-2" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-3" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0053.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 10px; height: 12px; vertical-align: -1px; margin-right: -0.057em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-1">S</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-parameter-based method for measuring the impedance of a symmetrical balanced antenna by using a two-port vector network analyzer (VNA) <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_2">[10]</a>. Two 50-<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-2-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-4" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 0.844em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.66em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-5" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-6" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/03A9.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 11px; height: 11px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-2">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> microstrip lines, which were etched onto a printed circuit board (PCB) and mounted back-to-back, were used as a test fixture to connect the antenna under test to a two-port VNA. The measurement system was calibrated at the end of the microstripe lines by using a set of special-purpose standards. It has been proven to be able to characterize the impedance of a symmetrical dipole antenna up to 1 GHz. Later, Duncan et al. developed the technique by replacing the microstrip lines with coaxial cables and using the standard calibration <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_2">[11]</a>. This technique had overcome the frequency limitation of the nonstandard calibration kits and made the measurement more convenient. However, using this method, the antenna impedance could not be extracted from the measured <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-3-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-7" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 0.664em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.604em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.6em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-8" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-9" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0053.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 10px; height: 12px; vertical-align: -1px; margin-right: -0.057em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-3">S</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-parameters directly. Another measurement must be carried out to find the network parameters of the coaxial cables. The deembedding of the influence of the cables from the measured <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-4-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-10" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 0.664em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.604em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.6em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-11" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-12" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0053.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 10px; height: 12px; vertical-align: -1px; margin-right: -0.057em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-4">S</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-parameters is complicated and tedious, including multiple parameter conversion of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-5-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-13" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 0.664em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.604em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.6em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-14" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-15" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0053.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 10px; height: 12px; vertical-align: -1px; margin-right: -0.057em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-5">S</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-parameters, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-6-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-16" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 3.246em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.886em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1002.89em 2.345em -999.997em); height: 11px; vertical-align: 0px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-19" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0042.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 12px; height: 11px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-20" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0043.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 12px; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-7">Y</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-parameters, as well as pre- and post-multiplication of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-8-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-25" role="math" style="display: inline-block; height: 11px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-29" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0043.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 12px; height: 11px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-8">ABCD</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-parameters.</p><p>The methodology presented in this paper is able to characterize the asymmetrical/symmetrical balanced antenna impedance precisely. Together with the coaxial fixture and the port-extension technique, the impedance of the antennas can be extracted directly from the measured <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-9-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-31" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 0.664em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.604em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.6em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-32" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-33" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0053.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 10px; height: 12px; vertical-align: -1px; margin-right: -0.057em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-9">S</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-parameters over broad frequency band.</p><div class="section_2" id="sec2a"><h3>A. Principle</h3><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 1(a)</a> shows a typical asymmetrical balanced dipole antenna, which is with two arms of different lengths and excited differentially. The positive and negative ports of the source with a voltage of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-10-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-34" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 0.844em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.72em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-35" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-36" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0056.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 12px; height: 12px; vertical-align: -1px; margin-right: -0.177em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.183em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-10">V</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are connected to the input terminals of the radiators of the antenna, respectively. As shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 1(b)</a>, the driven voltage can be split as <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-11-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-37" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 1.084em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.964em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.96em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-38" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-39" style="display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.544em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-41" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-42" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-43" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/238/0031.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 5px; height: 8px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.003em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-11">V_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-12-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-44" role="math" style="display: inline-block; Therefore, each terminal of the antenna radiators and the ground plane can be considered as a âport,â as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 1(c)</a>. The antenna can be equivalent to a âtwo-portâ network, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 2</a>. The impedance of the antenna is thus related to the network parameters of the equivalent two-port network, and can be characterized by measuring the network parameters such as <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-13-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-51" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 0.664em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.604em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.6em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-52" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-53" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0053.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 10px; height: 12px; vertical-align: -1px; margin-right: -0.057em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-13">S</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-parameters.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig1"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4806170/4806170-fig-1-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4806170/4806170-fig-1-small.gif" alt="Figure 1" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 1. </b><fig><p>Excitation and port definition of the asymmetrical balanced dipole antenna. <p></p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec2b"><h3>B. <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-14-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-54" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 0.73em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.626em; height: 0px; font-size: 112%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.302em 1000.61em 2.289em -999.98em); top: -2.128em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-55" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-56" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/400/0053.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 12px; height: 14px; vertical-align: 0px; margin-right: -0.049em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.055em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.133em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.055em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.934em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-14">S</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-Parameter Method</h3><p>From <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 2</a>, the normalized impedance of the antenna can be expressed as follows: <disp-formula id="deqn1" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><div class="MathJax_Display"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-15-Frame" tabindex="0" style="width: 100%;"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-57" role="math" style="display: inline-block; top: -4.021em; right: 0.003em;"><span class="mtd" id="mjx-eqn-${\hbox{(7)}}$" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-522" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-523" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-524" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-525" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-526" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-527" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-528" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-529" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0028.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 5px; height: 16px; vertical-align: -4px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0037.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 8px; height: 11px; vertical-align: 0px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0029.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 5px; height: 16px; vertical-align: -4px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -1.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 3.003em;"></span></span></nobr></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-31">Z_{d}={2Z_{0}\left(1-S_{11}^{2}+S_{21}^{2}-2S_{12}\right)\over(1-S_{11})^{2}-S_{21}^{2}}.\eqno{\hbox{(7)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">Z_{d}={2Z_{0}\left(1-S_{11}^{2}+S_{21}^{2}-2S_{12}\right)\over(1-S_{11})^{2}-S_{21}^{2}}.\eqno{\hbox{(7)}}</span></span></disp-formula></p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec2c"><h3>C. Measurement Setup</h3><p>The configuration of the measurement system is illustrated in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 3</a>. The measurement is conducted by using a two-port VNA (Agilent N5230A) and a test fixture. Any other VNA that features the port-extension function is suitable for the measurement. The test fixture is constructed by using two semiridge coaxial cables with a length of 100 mm and an outer conductor diameter of 2.2 mm. The coaxial cables are soldered together on their outer conductors. One end of the fixture is with two subminiature A (SMA) connectors and connected to the VNA through the test cables. The other end of the fixture is open with the small extensions of inner conductors to form the tips to connect the antenna under test.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig3"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4806170/4806170-fig-3-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4806170/4806170-fig-3-small.gif" alt="Figure 3" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 3. </b><fig><p>Measurement setup. (a) Schematic configuration. (b) Fixture prototype. (c) Measurement setup using Agilent N5230A network analyzer.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4806170/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec2d"><h3>D. Measurement Procedures</h3><p>It is recommended to conduct the measurement in an anechoic chamber or a place with controllable environment reflection. The measurement can be conducted via the following steps.
</p><ol><li><p>Conduct standard VNA parameters setting and calibration.</p></li><li><p>Shift the calibration plane through the port-extension technique to deembed the influence of the text fixture.</p><p>Connect the test fixture to the test cables and carry out the port extension to shift the calibration plane to the tips of the fixture. The fixture is required to be open or short circuited when performing the port extension. Short-circuited configuration (soldering the tips of the fixture and outer conductors of the coaxial cables together) is recommended since perfect âopenâ condition is very difficult to achieve, especially at higher frequencies.</p></li><li><p>Connect the antenna to the fixture and measure the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-32-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-601" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 0.664em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.604em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.6em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-602" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-603" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0053.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 10px; height: 12px; vertical-align: -1px; margin-right: -0.057em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-32">S</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-parameters.</p></li><li><p>Calculate the impedance of the antenna using <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn6" href="#deqn6" class="fulltext-link">(6)</a> or <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn7" href="#deqn7" class="fulltext-link">(7)</a>.</p></li></ol><p></p></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec3"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION III.</div><h2>Impedance Measurement Results</h2></div><p>To validate the measurement methodology, two types of balanced antennas, the asymmetrical dipole antenna and the symmetrical meander line dipole antenna, were prototyped and measured.</p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 4</a> shows the antenna prototypes and the detailed dimensions. All the antenna prototypes were printed onto an FR4 PCB with a dielectric constant of 4.4, a loss tangent of 0.02 and a thickness of 0.504 mm.</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig4"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4806170/4806170-fig-4-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4806170/4806170-fig-4-small.gif" alt="Figure 4" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 4. </b><fig><p>Antennas under test. (a) Asymmetrical dipole antenna. (b) Symmetrical meander line dipole antenna.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4806170/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 5</a> illustrates the measured and simulated impedance of the asymmetrical dipole antenna over a frequency range of 500â1500 MHz. One of the dipole antenna arms is 100 mm in length and the other is 60 mm. The width of the arms is 10 mm. The simulation was conducted with IE3D software, which is based on the method of moments <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref13" id="context_ref_13_3">[13]</a>. Very good agreement has been observed for both real and imaginary parts of the impedance. The capability of measuring the impedance of asymmetrical balanced antenna is conducive to RFID tag antenna design, wherein asymmetrical antennas are normally configured to match the specific ASIC chip.</p><p>
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig5"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4806170/4806170-fig-5-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4806170/4806170-fig-5-small.gif" alt="Figure 5" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 5. </b><fig><p>Measured and simulated impedance of the asymmetrical dipole antenna. (a) Real part. (b) Imaginary part.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4806170/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 6</a> compares the measured and simulated impedance of the symmetrical meander line dipole antenna. Both measured real and imaginary parts of the impedance show good agreement with the simulation across the frequency range of 800â1000 MHz.
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig6"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4806170/4806170-fig-6-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4806170/4806170-fig-6-small.gif" alt="Figure 6" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 6. </b><fig><p>Measured and simulated impedance of the symmetrical meander line dipole antenna. (a) Real part. (b) Imaginary part.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4806170/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec4"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION IV.</div><h2>Example in RFID Tag Co-Design</h2></div><div class="section_2" id="sec4a"><h3>A. Applications and Design Considerations</h3><p>Considering the specific RFID application in a Sushi restaurant, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 7</a>, the tagged plastic Sushi plates are to be detected by a portable RFID reader for automatic billing and tracking the favorite dishes for customers. The tags are attached at the bottom of the plastic plate of a diameter of 150 mm and a height of 15 mm. There is a concaved portion (rim) at the bottom of the plate, wherein the RFID tag will be affixed. The rim is with an inner diameter of 85 mm and a height of 10 mm.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig7"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4806170/4806170-fig-7-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4806170/4806170-fig-7-small.gif" alt="Figure 7" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 7. </b><fig><p>RFID applications in Sushi restaurants: plate tracking.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4806170/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>The embedded tags are required to be detected by the RFID reader with an adequate distance at any angle in the azimuth plane. The major design considerations of such a tag antenna include achieving omnidirectional radiation pattern and proper impedance matching for maximizing the system reading range and enhancing the system reliability. In addition, a small and flat profile is also very desirable for easy attachment to the plates.</p><p>The tag is required to be designed at the UHF band of the 920â925-MHz band for the applications in Singapore. It can, of course, be easily tuned to other frequency bands for the applications in different regions. The ASIC used here is Impinj-Monza 2 with an impedance of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-33-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-604" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 5.529em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.988em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.93em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-605" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-606" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0035.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; height: 11px; vertical-align: 0px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0039.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; height: 11px; vertical-align: 0px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-607" style="display: inline-block; padding-left: 0.243em;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/2212.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 11px; height: 1px; vertical-align: 3px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-608" style="display: inline-block; padding-left: 0.243em;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/006A.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; height: 14px; vertical-align: -3px; margin-left: 0.003em; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-609" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0032.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; height: 11px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0034.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; height: 11px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0032.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; height: 11px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-610" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/00A0.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 0px; height: 0px; margin-right: 0.243em;" /></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-611" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/03A9.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 11px; height: 11px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-33">59-j242\ \Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.<a ref-type="fn" anchor="fn1" class="footnote-link"><sup>1</sup></a></p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec4b"><h3>B. Tag Antenna Design without Considering Plate Effect</h3><p>To realize omnidirectional reading pattern, a folded dipole antenna shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 8</a> is proposed <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref14" id="context_ref_14_4b">[14]</a>. The folded antenna configuration offers desired omnidirectional radiation in the azimuth plane. In addition, the impedance of the antenna is easily tuned to meet the specified requirements by changing the dimensions of the folded arms of the antenna.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig8"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4806170/4806170-fig-8-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4806170/4806170-fig-8-small.gif" alt="Figure 8" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 8. </b><fig><p>Geometry of the proposed omnidirectional tag antenna.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4806170/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>The tag antenna was first designed without considering the plastic plate to validate the omnidirectional reading performance. The tag was prototyped on a 0.5-mm thin FR4 substrate. Using an SAMSys MP9320 EPC reader with output power of 1 W or 30 dBm (the output power can be adjusted by adding external attenuators) and a dipole antenna with gain of 2 dBi as the reader antenna, the reading range of the tag was tested in free space, and the result is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 9</a> and indicated by solid line. The reading range of the tag is 10â14 cm in free space with reader output of 25 mW. The tag was then affixed at the bottom of the plastic plate, the reading range, as shown in the <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 9</a> (dashed line), exhibits dramatic reduction to 2.5â4.0 cm even with larger reader output power of 100 mW.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig9"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4806170/4806170-fig-9-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4806170/4806170-fig-9-small.gif" alt="Figure 9" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 9. </b><fig><p>Comparison of reading patterns of the RFID tag without/with plastic plate.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4806170/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec4c"><h3>C. Co-Design and Optimization</h3><p>The performance degradation of the tag when attached to the plastic plate is caused by the loading effect of the plastic plate. The loading effect changes the input impedance of the tag antenna at the operating frequencies, and thus results in mismatch between the antenna and the ASIC. In addition, the lossy plastic material causes the efficiency reduction of tag antenna. To optimize the embedded tag performance, the tag antenna must be co-designed with the plastic plate by taking the loading effect of the plastic plate into consideration. However, it is very challenging to execute the co-design in practical scenarios because it is difficult to characterize the electrical properties of the plastic plate accurately, and thus, the predication of the performance of the antenna especially its impedance by simulation is hardly possible.</p><p>A plastic substrate was added underneath the tag antenna in simulation to imitate the plastic plate. The plastic substrate was assigned a thickness of 5 mm, a dielectric constant of 2, and a loss tangent of 0.02. Based on the simulation, the antenna was prototyped; the reading range of the newly designed tag has been increased to 6.0â9.5 cm with reader output power of 100 mW.</p><p>However, the read range is still far from the requirement. It is clear that the co-design of the tag by a simulation approach cannot achieve optimal performance since the impedance of the tag antenna cannot be characterized accurately with presumed electrical parameters.</p><p>To characterize the antenna impedance precisely, the tag antenna, together with the plastic plate, was measured as illustrated in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig10" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 10</a>. The measured and simulated impedance are exhibited in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig11" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 11</a>. A frequency shift of 120 MHz is observed. In addition, the measured real and imaginary parts of the impedance are with smaller amplitude than simulated ones. It implies that dielectric constant and loss tangent of the plastic plate are underestimated.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig10"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4806170/4806170-fig-10-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4806170/4806170-fig-10-small.gif" alt="Figure 10" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 10. </b><fig><p>Impedance measurement of the tag antenna together with the plastic plate.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4806170/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig11"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4806170/4806170-fig-11-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4806170/4806170-fig-11-small.gif" alt="Figure 11" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 11. </b><fig><p>Comparison of the calculated and measured impedance of the tag antenna together with the plastic plate. The plastic plate is with assumed parameters of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-34-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-612" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 3.442em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.715em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.326em 1002.65em 2.517em -999.997em); height: 7px; vertical-align: 0px; margin-right: 0.069em;" /></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 3.972em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.833em; left: 0.466em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-616" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-617" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-618" style="display: inline-block; height: 4px; vertical-align: 2px; margin-right: 0.069em;" /></span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-627" style="display: inline-block; padding-left: 0.268em;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0030.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; height: 2px; margin-right: 0.069em;" /><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0030.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; height: 11px; margin-right: 0.069em;" /></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.186em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.079em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.171em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-35">\tan\delta=0.02</script></tex-math></inline-formula> in simulation.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4806170/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>Based on the measured results, the frequency shift and amplitude variation of the impedance have been considered in advance in simulation. The antenna was retuned and validated by measurement. Finally, good impedance matching was achieved with the measured return loss of â15 dB at 923 MHz. The optimized antenna prototype is with the dimensions: <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-36-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-628" role="math" style="display: inline-block; <p></p></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec5"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION V.</div><h2>Conclusions</h2></div><p>An experimental methodology for the characterization of the impedance of the balanced RFID tag antennas has been proposed and its application in a co-designing RFID tag with platforms has been demonstrated. Using a two-port VNA and the port-extension technique, the impedance of the symmetrical and asymmetrical balanced tag antennas can be extracted from the measured <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-51-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-879" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 0.664em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.604em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.6em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-880" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-881" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0053.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 10px; height: 12px; vertical-align: -1px; margin-right: -0.057em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-51">S</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-parameters directly.</p><p>The proposed methodology is promising and useful for RFID tag co-design with practical environments to enhance RFID system performance. The example of co-designing and optimizing the UHF RFID tag with the plastic Sushi plate has demonstrated the advantage of the methodology. The impedance characteristics of the tag antenna together with a plastic plate has been accurately characterized, and the conjugate matching between the tag antenna and the ASIC has been realized so that the reading range of the RFID system has been greatly enhanced.</p></div>
<h3>ACKNOWLEDGMENT</h3><p>The authors would like to thank I. J. Lukas, Kenetics Innovation Pte Ltd., Singapore, for his work in RFID tag design.</p></div></div>
</div><!-- end ngIf: ft.sectionText -->

<script>

function getCookie(name) {
	var nameEQ = name + "=";
	var ca = document.cookie.split(';');
	for(var i=0;i &lt; ca.length;i++) {
		var c = ca[i];
		while (c.charAt(0)==' ') c = c.substring(1,c.length);
		if (c.indexOf(nameEQ) == 0) return c.substring(nameEQ.length,c.length);
	}
	return null;
}

		}
	}
});

The balanced tag antenna is considered as a two-port network and the impedance of the antenna is characterized using network parameters. In the measurement, the antenna is connected to the two ports of a vector network analyzer through a test fixture.
